  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e933007d-5234-441c-818c-be2f204aabb6'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer358788251888850064">The Others freed the <i>cassandra sangue</i> to protect the blood prophets from exploitation, not realizing their actions would have dire consequences. Now the fragile seers are in greater danger than ever before; both from their own weaknesses and from those who seek to control their divinations for wicked purposes.   <span id="freeText358788251888850064" style="display:none">The Others freed the <i>cassandra sangue</i> to protect the blood prophets from exploitation, not realizing their actions would have dire consequences. Now the fragile seers are in greater danger than ever before; both from their own weaknesses and from those who seek to control their divinations for wicked purposes. In desperate need of answers, Simon Wolfgard, a shape-shifter leader among the Others, has no choice but to enlist blood prophet Meg Corbyn’s help, regardless of the risks she faces by aiding him.<br /><br />Meg is still deep in the throes of her addiction to the euphoria she feels when she cuts and speaks prophecy. She knows each slice of her blade tempts death. But Others and humans alike need answers, and her visions may be Simon’s only hope of ending the conflict.<br /><br />For the shadows of war are deepening across the Atlantik, and the prejudice of a fanatic faction is threatening to bring the battle right to Meg and Simon’s doorstep…</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=favorite-series">favorite-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1184342181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9713744527630357655">Up until now I had been giving the books in this series four stars? Why? Maybe because I'm stingy with the stars? Maybe because I'm stoopid?!<br/>I'm breaking down and giving the stars. This is probably the best paranormal fiction I have read. I admit it.<br/><br/><b>There are more storms coming. Big storms. Bad storms. We need to make this place work.</b><br/><br/>That's the biggest question in this book. Can the "Others" keep living with the humans. After the humans act like dumbasses with the Humans First movement.<br/><a href='http://imgur.com/ZfdkXJL' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427225993i/14251036.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>The w</span>
  <span id="freeText9713744527630357655" style="display:none">Up until now I had been giving the books in this series four stars? Why? Maybe because I'm stingy with the stars? Maybe because I'm stoopid?!<br>I'm breaking down and giving the stars. This is probably the best paranormal fiction I have read. I admit it.<br><br><b>There are more storms coming. Big storms. Bad storms. We need to make this place work.</b><br><br>That's the biggest question in this book. Can the "Others" keep living with the humans. After the humans act like dumbasses with the Humans First movement.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/ZfdkXJL" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1427225993i/14251036.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>The world building in these books is big and I've gotten attached to several of the characters and every book I whine that I want more of that character. I do understand when books have this much going on that you can only give the reader so much. I think instead of 400 page books these should go on to be 800 page puppy squishers..and I would still eat them up.<br>It's fun watching Meg's character grow. It's only been a few months since she escaped the controller and the Others are allowing her to grow into her own person. Sometimes I got aggravated with her and felt she was Mary Sue-ing but then the other characters jumped in a snapped her little whiny ass back into the character I love.<br>Watching the human "pack" interact with the Others is tons of fun too.<br><b>A pack of human females and some Crows in a building full of things to buy. He sat back and sighed. "And humans think vampires are scary."</b><br><br>The story still doesn't move along as fast as some books do but then it really didn't cause me to glaze my eyes over in boredom. Bishop kept my attention so much that I didn't even realize that I was at the end of the book. That rarely happens. I completely have steeped into this world and I love every single second of it. Must have this object too. Completely fangirling....<br><a href="http://imgur.com/TXU8q3h" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br> Now I have to wait a year for the next installment?!!?!?! Unacceptable. WANTS MORE!<br><a href="http://imgur.com/W0Wo0dd" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br>I'm thinking this story instead of the whole sexy vampire/werewolf thing should have became the norm. Because it's awesome.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/jNqIqDS" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1306298995" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1306298995" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1306298995?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">PNR fans who don't need sexxytimes</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library-kindle">my-library-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=shifter">shifter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1306298995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12190851926390904420">From the blog at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2015/06/21/vision-in-silver-by-anne-bishop-or-i-shamelessly-promote-my-reviews/'>https://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2015/...</a> where I had a lot of fun playing link-to-my-review.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434684813i/15253014._SX540_.jpg' width='280' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I cannot effing believe how much this series is like candy for my brain. Really; utterly predictable, but clearly engineered to hit that magic trifecta of sugar, fat and salt. Read and could not put it down. I'm not even bothered by the filling I now need.<br/><br/>*************<br/><br/>Ok, feelz out of the way, I spent some time on a thoughtful review:<br/><br/>Three hundred posts has given, at the very least, persp</span>
  <span id="freeText12190851926390904420" style="display:none">From the blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2015/06/21/vision-in-silver-by-anne-bishop-or-i-shamelessly-promote-my-reviews/">https://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2015/...</a> where I had a lot of fun playing link-to-my-review.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434684813i/15253014._SX540_.jpg" width="280" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I cannot effing believe how much this series is like candy for my brain. Really; utterly predictable, but clearly engineered to hit that magic trifecta of sugar, fat and salt. Read and could not put it down. I'm not even bothered by the filling I now need.<br><br>*************<br><br>Ok, feelz out of the way, I spent some time on a thoughtful review:<br><br>Three hundred posts has given, at the very least, perspective on why a particular book may or may not appeal to me. As I wrote in my review of the surprisingly ghastly <i>The Diviners</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/590828506" rel="nofollow noopener">(review)</a>, "I tend to read for three things: plot, character and language. Usually at least one can sustain me through a book" (You see, I'm citing myself so I don't turn into Jonah Lehrer <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1239768284" rel="nofollow noopener">[review]</a>). Anne Bishop's The Others series is light on all three, and yet it is the Pringles in my reading world: I can't put them down. <br><br>I should dislike this. The plot nominally revolves around a twenty-four year-old woman who is astonishingly naive. Normally, this would cause at least a small eye roll, but the context is that until six months ago, she’s been confined against her will, her life structured and optimized to divine the future when her her skin is cut and blood drawn. Actually, her innocence to behavior subtleties becomes a clever narrative device, allowing her to seek explanations along with the reader. <br><br>Many reviews rave on the world building, but I've found it glaringly incomplete--good heavens, it's odd. If Sanderson gave the impression of having created the world before writing a plot in <i>The Way of Kings</i> <a href="&lt;a%20href=" rel="nofollow noopener">(review)</a>, Bishop seems to be discovering it in context of plotting. Inconsistencies appear, but because Bishop spends so little time on the details, I’ve managed not to dwell on them either.<br><br>Consider: The Others are a lifeform native to America (or whatever Bishop calls it, but since it has the Atlantik Ocean and five Great Lakes, let’s go with America). Currently, many Others live in Courtyards in large human cities, similar to embassies. There are small human communities as well, particularly ones around farming settlements. However, The Others control all the land, leasing it to the humans, with wild spaces between communities for their more wild brethren. But humans mine, farm, log, ship, and presumably, work in the steel mills they mention. Trains run between communities. Ships sail the oceans. Snowmobiles and golf carts exist. There are also cars, electric lights, email, computers, videos, cellphones and telephones. Not mentioned is the corollary that there are rubber plantations, power plants, cobalt mines, movie studios, satellites and telephone lines. Questions: why does news take so long to travel? Why do The Others have to take trains with humans to get from community to community instead of emailing, calling or using their other form? Why does Bishop continually call attention to The Others rescinding leases for pollution without recognizing those industries are all ‘dirty’? There’s enough cars to cause accidents. At the same time there’s all these normal/current resources, why are The Others concerned with understanding the human community? Haven’t they already understood it enough if they can drive, use computers, lease land, have Other-focused movies and Other-focused books?<br><br><b>It’s a mess, I tell you.</b> I mostly accept it, and in this book, even grew to appreciate it as Simon, the leader of The Others in Lakeside, wonders if The Others taking human form are going to evolve into the replacement for the humans. I’ve also assumed that Bishop was hinting at technological developments that would win the war against The Others, such as airplanes and mass-produced weapons. But guns are already in play in this society–hunters are talked about in the first book, and this book points out that one of the fearsome Others needs to be in a certain range in order to harvest life, and being wounded by a gun is possible. So sure, it’s clear humans can’t win against earthquakes, tornadoes and snowstorms, but are The Others ready to lose the more corporeal-based lifeforms, and why are they so innocent about the risks humans present? And holy distractions–are The Others really any different from humans if they enjoy hanging out in front of a movie with some popcorn??<br><br>Lazy world-building aside, characterization is not particularly layered either. It’s an ensemble cast and Bishop commits the crime of repetitive description, adding little information time they appear. Crows like “shiny,” Tess’ hair turns color with her mood, wolves growl when they are irritated, spirits have the characteristics of their namesake (‘Winter,’ ‘Spring’). Monty, one of the policemen, gets the most chance to develop when we meet his family. Meg, the blood prophet, shows a little character growth, although there’s some not-so-slick reverse engineering allowing it (after 6 months outside her compound, she suddenly discovers too much sensory detail is ‘overwhelming’ and she’ll ‘shut down’). Other than that, the narrative character-switching mostly gives the reader the sense that something is happening, when really, it is isn’t. At least not in a large way. Personally, I have the feeling that Bishop was trying to get the reader to the point where such shifts in world-view would seem seismic. They didn’t, of course, but they did seem significant.<br><br>More significantly, there's a lot of chauvinism in this book. Males are leaders, enforcers, and spiritual gurus, whether Others (Simon, Eliot, Blair, Nathan, Henry) or humans (governor, mayor, cult leader, policeman). Women are the balancing act, the emotion, the social glue that keeps things running, soothes chaos and can be diverted by movies, yoga and jewelry. Most readers won't complain about the chauvinism because it is of the Noble Knight School of Sexism, where strong men protect the young/women, broker the deals, do the investigating, the fighting and the traveling. Men are predators. Yes, yes--this book has a scene that has an exception to this. One. I was thinking about this again because a normal real wolf pack always has females, particularly a very dominant one as co-leader, and there are no female wolves present in this situation. It's clear that there is a very gentle, growing relationship between Meg and Simon, so a lack of female balance keeps the social relationships focused on where Bishop wants it. But it is notable for me as another area that usually results in a serious amount of annoyance--particularly when done by Jim Butcher <a href="&lt;a%20href=" rel="nofollow noopener">(reveiew)</a>.<br><br>And the writing. I’d give it tenth grade level, give or take. Simple structure, straight-forward punctuation and very few superlatives. The simplicity fits with Simon and Meg’s voices, but the rest of the time? I suspect that because so much of it is dialogue-focused, it isn’t as noticeable. Still, as I enjoy a vivid descriptor (note the ‘beautiful language’ tag on my page), so I find it interesting that this doesn’t bore me:<br><br> <i> “Meg didn’t remember much about the storm that struck Lakeside after she’d fallen through the ice on the creek. But she remembered being stuck in the hospital… because the whole city had been trapped by a record snowfall… Crows followed them as they continued down the road. Hawks soared overhead or found a convenient observation perch. A couple of Owls, who should have been home by now, flew over their heads.”</i><br><br>So it’s clear, right? I should be vehemently opposed to reading this, but I can’t stop–it’s so delicious! After I finished this one, I started <i>re-reading it the next day.</i> And finished it again. Sure, there’s problems, but nothing really has pushed me into full eye-roll. I also remain intrigued because it’s the only UF I’ve read so far that treats humans like inferior citizens and hints at an upcoming disaster. I can only conclude that Bishop has hit the taste trifecta of ideal composition of Sugar, Salt and Fat <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/561437941" rel="nofollow noopener">(review)</a>.<br><br><br>Three and a half Other stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="12190851926390904420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_984311212" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/984311212" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/984311212?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=amazing-writing">amazing-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=all-the-right-choices">all-the-right-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2014">arc-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=glistening-fangs">glistening-fangs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=my-flat-army">my-flat-army</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=werewhatevers">werewhatevers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2014">reviewed-in-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=best-of-2015">best-of-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer984311212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13033883019101551191"><br/>Three five-star ratings for three books in this series, that’s pretty much all you need to know before running to the bookstore to get your own copies of all three available books. But if you need more convincing (as I usually do), I’m more than happy to sing praise until I go hoarse. Or lose a finger typing. You get my point.<br/><br/>Here it is in no uncertain terms: The Others, Anne Bishop’s fantasy series, is brilliant, no two ways about it. Her worldbuilding is extraordinary, her characters fascinati</span>
  <span id="freeText13033883019101551191" style="display:none"><br>Three five-star ratings for three books in this series, that’s pretty much all you need to know before running to the bookstore to get your own copies of all three available books. But if you need more convincing (as I usually do), I’m more than happy to sing praise until I go hoarse. Or lose a finger typing. You get my point.<br><br>Here it is in no uncertain terms: The Others, Anne Bishop’s fantasy series, is brilliant, no two ways about it. Her worldbuilding is extraordinary, her characters fascinating, and even the tiniest details of her plots are thought through. So many things happen at once, but nothing is random and nothing is without significance for our Meg and the <i>terra indigene</i>. Bishop has many successful novels behind her and her experience is evident on every page, her control over her story absolute. <br><br><i>Vision in Silver</i> brings us back to the wonderful (albeit violent) world of Thaisia. Meg faces new challenges while adapting to her life in the Courtyard, and she needs to be strong enough to help not only herself, but the other blood prophets as well. Luckily for her and the rest of the <i>cassandra sangue</i> she has both determination and Simon’s unwavering support. <br><br>The human police are working more closely with the Others despite facing repercussions from the Humans First and Last movement. The HFL is becoming stronger by the day, constantly working to turn the public against the Others (not that they have to work very hard), spreading lies and bold misinterpretations of events, blaming the <i>terra indigene</i> for everything from hunger to bad weather. Being a so-called Wolf lover is becoming more and more difficult in Thaisia, and the humans working in the Courtyard are going through a very tough time.<br><br>Simon, being the progressive leader he is, certainly won’t allow the Courtyard humans to suffer for their allegiances. After all, his Meg needs her human pack, and everything Meg needs, Simon doesn’t hesitate to provide. <br><br>With her childlike view of the world, Meg is a very interesting character, but I found Simon even more fascinating this time around. He has the instincts of an animal and the astuteness of the most successful businessman, but he often fails to understand the human way of things. He tries, though, mostly because understanding humans means understanding and helping his Meg, but the process is slow and often hilarious. These two are slowly finding their way to each other. They are, for all intents and purposes, in a relationship, even if they don’t seem to realize it. They practically live together and mostly act like an old married couple, but the way they show their affection is somewhat different from what we’d expect.<br><br>And that is precisely what I adore about the series. Bishop never lets us forget that Simon Wolfgard is wolf and <i>only</i> wolf. His kind has learned to live in human skin, at least temporarily, but they find it extremely uncomfortable and tend to avoid it if at all possible. Simon thinks like a wolf and acts like a wolf, and his understanding of humans is minimal. He sees the monkeys, as he calls us, mostly as prey, with only a few exceptions in the Courtyard itself. This series is basically about the clash of two cultures. Two species that have a history of horrible violence to each other are trying to find a way to live together in peace. Their differences are huge, but if there’s enough common ground, thanks to Simon Wolfgard and Meg Corbyn, they might just succeed.<br><br>Read this. That is all.<br><br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13033883019101551191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review984311212">

<div id="review_1856822490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1856822490" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1856822490?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1856822490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9878480793317069409">So much is wrong with this book. Hell, this entire <i>series</i>!<br/><b>BUT I CAN'T STOP READING.</b><br/>It's so frustrating to <i>know</i> on an intellectual level that there are multiple plot holes <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Why are the humans suddenly unafraid to mock Others in public? A month or so ago, the wolves would literally EAT anyone who wandered across their fence and serve the human meat in their butcher shop. They couldn't get anyone reliable to work for them, because all the humans were too freaked out by what went on in</span></span>
  <span id="freeText9878480793317069409" style="display:none">So much is wrong with this book. Hell, this entire <i>series</i>!<br><b>BUT I CAN'T STOP READING.</b><br>It's so frustrating to <i>know</i> on an intellectual level that there are multiple plot holes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Why are the humans suddenly unafraid to mock Others in public? A month or so ago, the wolves would literally EAT anyone who wandered across their fence and serve the human meat in their butcher shop. They couldn't get anyone reliable to work for them, because all the humans were too freaked out by what went on in there. But <i>NOW</i> the Others are under attack and nobody is afraid of them? I kinda doubt that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, several unbelievably convenient developments to further the story <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Meg's suddenly overwhelmed by too much stimulus...now? After months of living in the Courtyard...<i>now</i> she suddenly has panic attacks if something in her office is moved? She gets dizzy if she goes into one of the stores that sell postcards and office supplies? Are you fucking kidding me with this shit? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and characters who all seem to be incredibly naive about the world they live in <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ How do the vast majority of Others not know the basic things about how to buy goods and interact with humans? If the only reason they're allowing humans to exist is because they like the stuff they make, then shouldn't they USE more of the stuff they make on a regular basis? Or be more curious about how to get that stuff? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br><br><b>I love these books, but if I start scratching the surface of the story...</b><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483712265ra/21641905.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Besides my spoilery complaints, I get a bit frustrated with the way the characters think and speak. The Crows with their obsession with <i>Shiny</i> is a good example. I think it's supposed to make them seem to have a more animalistic nature, but it just makes them sound mentally retarded. And I have the same problem with Meg and Simon sometimes. Both of them seem so...un-adult!<br>Listening to Meg is like listening to an awkward 10 year old, and listening to Simon is what I imagine listening to a (somewhat) lovable junkyard dog sounds like.<br><i>sigh</i><br>I've never been happier that a relationship was moving along at such a slow pace because I don't think either of them has <i>any</i> idea about what they're doing. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483715107ra/21642445.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So with all of my complaints, why should you read this?<br>No idea.<br>But you SHOULD. I don't know what it is about Bishop's series that fascinates me, but I've been binge-reading these suckers for a few weeks now, and I just can't get enough!<br>Sometimes there's no logical explanation for why you love something...<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483716048ra/21642595.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, the short and skinny version of <b>Vision in Silver</b>? It's about the other Blood Prophets like Meg, and Monty and his daughter Lizzy.<br>They <i>all</i> need to be saved from the Humans First and Last (HFL) movement, and the Others from Lakeside decide it's their job to protect them. <br>Craziness ensues, new characters are introduced, and the humans get one step closer to annihilation. I <i>love</i> it! What am I going to do when I finish the next book in a few days, and have to <b>wait</b> for #5 to come out?! <br><i>sobs</i><br><b>FANTASTIC STUFF!</b><br>Go on, eat the candy...<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483716211ra/21642608.gif" width="400" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1116256577" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1116256577" />
    <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata"><img alt="Faye, la Patata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557835753p2/7650833.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1116256577?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faye, la Patata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faye, la Patata" href="/user/show/7650833-faye-la-patata">Faye, la Patata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=someone-hold-me">someone-hold-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=adult-but-no-sex">adult-but-no-sex</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=best-books-i-ve-ever-read">best-books-i-ve-ever-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=slow-and-steady-romance">slow-and-steady-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7650833-faye-la-patata?shelf=animals">animals</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1116256577" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10211695976967365195">Make way, make way, for the newest installment of the best Urban Fantasy is now upon us. I shit you not, folks, <em>The Others</em> is still going strong, and no doubt it would continue to be so in the years to come. <strong>If I ever had one wish for the literary world, it would be this: that Anne Bishop would never,<em> ever</em> tire of writing about this complex, fantastic world, because when that day comes, I fear it would be the day my heart would wilt and die.</strong> I wish I were kidding, but I seriously love this serie</span>
  <span id="freeText10211695976967365195" style="display:none">Make way, make way, for the newest installment of the best Urban Fantasy is now upon us. I shit you not, folks, <em>The Others</em> is still going strong, and no doubt it would continue to be so in the years to come. <strong>If I ever had one wish for the literary world, it would be this: that Anne Bishop would never,<em> ever</em> tire of writing about this complex, fantastic world, because when that day comes, I fear it would be the day my heart would wilt and die.</strong> I wish I were kidding, but I seriously love this series that damn much.<br /><br />I know I've said this again and again, but it demands to be repeated: I loved <em>Written in Red </em>and <i>Murder of Crows</i>, the first and second books of this series. <strong>They were fun, beautiful, and riveting reads that made me turn pages like a lunatic, so engrossed in the stories, politics, and dynamics in the Lakeside Courtyard.</strong> It made me want to ditch my human skin and join these shapeshifting creatures, as they are definitely more fun than all these grouchy, greedy humans (if you read this, you will understand what I mean!). <strong>I expected <em>Vision in Silver</em> to be as good, but it actually went beyond everything that I could ever hope for. I didn't think it was possible, but this third book might just be my favorite yet!</strong><br /><br />The political intrigue that started in <em>Written in Red</em> concerning the issues between the humans and the terra indigene continues to grow here in book 3, the tension and violence ever-more increasing, especially with the appearance of Lizzy, the daughter of police officer Monty, who may have jumpstarted a controversial string of events when she escaped a particularly difficult situation. <strong>It was so intense to see everything play out here - from how our friends at Howling Good Reads reacted, to how they took charge, even to how the humans attempted to manipulate them to take the upper hand!</strong> The plot points here were seriously so interesting to read as it effectively portrayed how far a specie can go when they think it's for their own survival. Seeing everything go down to the ending was such a roller coaster ride that I still can't forget it up to this day. Needless to say, when it ended, my mind was still reeling from the impact of it.<br /><br />And it's not just that, the world here grows as well. <strong>There is a deep sense of mystery present as soon as the book hints at hidden terra indigene, too powerful and too old to even imagine and comprehend.</strong> They aren't really there in a traditional, physical sense, but their presence and power and influence simply jump from the pages, making you feel mystified and, weirdly, humbled. It's so weird how that happened, but when I came to that point, I just really felt small simply from how even Simon was scared of them... whoever "them" might be. This made me only excited to see what else is in store for us.<strong> I love how Bishop knows which kind of information to withhold, making us yearn for them... and when she discloses them, it hits us like a pick-up truck and our minds are left reeling, unable to compute the information given.</strong> She is <strong>
  <em>that</em>
</strong> good.<br /><br />And the relationship! My SHIIIP! <strong>Simon and Meg continue to grow here as individuals and as friends</strong> (or maybe soon-to-be-lovers? YES, PLEASE!), taking their time as they discover more about each other and about themselves. <strong>How they affected other in many ways is even more pronounced here, and what is even better is that they are slowly becoming conscious of it, and my gods, IT IS DELICIOUS. </strong>I just love their dynamics, the gestures here and there that are small but are so precious and meaningful. They come from different backgrounds, from different species altogether, but the chemistry IS RIGHT OVER THERE and it's so interesting to see how their differences translate when it comes to their interactions with each other and with other people (or creatures, mehehe).<br /><br /><strong>Long story short, this series and this book is perfection and don't believe anyone saying otherwise. :P</strong><br /><br /><strong><em>Visions in Silver</em> is a VERY strong continuation of a series that is known for its amazing, likeable, and unique cast of characters and its world that is so vast, different, and eerily-familiar, all at the same time.</strong> If you haven't started this one yet (or the series in general), you're missing out and I implore you to get your copies now.<br /><br /><br />------------------<br />Post-reading:<br /><br /><b>LOVE LOVE LOVE LOVE LOVE LOVE LOVE LOVE LOVE LOVE</b><br /><br />It is one of my fervent wishes to live in Lakeside Courtyard. It amazes me everyday how Anne Bishop is able to create a world so brutal and so charming at the same time. To be honest, I love this installment the most. Finally some progress between two awesome characters, we get to see a little more of the world while still being mysterious at the same time, and, oh, a lot of special meat. MIAM.<br /><br />In any case, if you loved the last two books and are eagerly waiting for this one, I GUARANTEE YOU THAT IT WILL NOT DISAPPOINT. NON NON NON. YOU WILL LOVE IT TO BITS.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10211695976967365195" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2998183606" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer9372403687385546305"><b>The time</b> to write a full-length review for this book I do not have, ergo <b>severely cut the crap shall be</b>. Must be your lucky day and stuff.<br/><br/><b><u>Why this book should have been most ruthlessly buried in the unfathomable depths of my DNF graveyard</u>:</b><br/><br/>① <b>Nothing happens</b>.<br/><br/>② <b>Nothing happens</b>.<br/><br/>③ Once in a while, <b>nothing happens</b>. <br/><br/>④ Some authors write <b>slow-paced books</b>. Anne Bishop writes <b>no-pace books</b>. Because <b>
  <i>nothing happens</i>
</b> = no action = <b>no need for pacing and stuff</b> = tada!<br/><br/>⑤ <b>World building</b> is vague as fish! The</span>
  <span id="freeText9372403687385546305" style="display:none"><b>The time</b> to write a full-length review for this book I do not have, ergo <b>severely cut the crap shall be</b>. Must be your lucky day and stuff.<br><br><b><u>Why this book should have been most ruthlessly buried in the unfathomable depths of my DNF graveyard</u>:</b><br><br>① <b>Nothing happens</b>.<br><br>② <b>Nothing happens</b>.<br><br>③ Once in a while, <b>nothing happens</b>. <br><br>④ Some authors write <b>slow-paced books</b>. Anne Bishop writes <b>no-pace books</b>. Because <b>
  <i>nothing happens</i>
</b> = no action = <b>no need for pacing and stuff</b> = tada!<br><br>⑤ <b>World building</b> is vague as fish! There are <b>inconsistencies</b> aplenty! <b>Plot holes</b> abound! Yay!<br><br>⑥ <b><s>Some</s> Most of the characters</b> act as if they were (choose all <s>that apply</s>):<br><b>a</b>) On the <b>spectrum</b> <br><b>b</b>) Slightly <s>moronic</s> <b>simple-minded</b> <br><b>c</b>) <b>Naïve</b> as shrimp, <b>ever-bewildered</b> 10-year-olds <br><b>d</b>) a<br><b>e</b>) b<br><b>f</b>) c<br><b>g</b>) <b>all of the above</b><br><br>⑦ Some authors write <b>slow-burn romances</b>. Anne Bishop writes <b>no-burn romances</b>. She takes things so bloody shrimping slow, <b>nothing burns</b>! Yay! Not a chance you’ll get “Boom! Pregnant!” while reading this book! Yay! It’s the <b>most efficient contraceptive ever</b>! Yay!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1558909720ra/27576037.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>That’s Simon, Nathan and Sam in their Halloween costumes, in case you were wondering.</i><br><br><b><u>Why I ended up lurving this book against my better (albeit slightly nefarious) judgment</u>:</b> <br><br>① The <b>world building</b> might be lazy as shrimp, but the idea at its core is bloody fishing <b>refreshing and original and creative and stuff</b>. (A world in which <b>murderous creatures ruthlessly rule over lowly mortals</b>? Talk about a dream come true.) <br><br>② <b><s>Some</s> Most of the characters</b> act as if they were (choose all <s>that apply</s>):<br><b>a</b>) On the <b>spectrum</b> <br><b>b</b>) Slightly <s>moronic</s> <b>simple-minded</b> <br><b>c</b>) <b>Naïve</b> as shrimp 10-year-olds <br><b>d</b>) a<br><b>e</b>) b<br><b>f</b>) c<br><b>g</b>) <b>all of the above</b><br><br><i>Sorry, what? I already said that in the cons section? And your point is? Cons can be pros and vice-versa and stuff. Besides, socially inept <s>beasts</s> characters are <b>Super Extra Hot</b> (SEH™), if you ask me.</i><br><br>② The <b><s>communication issues</s> interactions</b> between the Others and the puny humans are <b>everything</b>. They remind me of <i>my</i> <b>slightly frustrating, moderately baffling, eye-roll inducing dealings</b> with homo sapiens weaklings. Which might or might not explain why I find this series <b>most entertaining</b> and stuff.<br><br>③ <i>“Do you know what happened to the dinosaurs? <b>The Others is what happened to the dinosaurs</b>.”</i><br><br><b>Hahahahahaha</b>. Gotta love <i>terra indigene</i> humor. Such great <b>stand up comics</b> they’d make. (Not sure puny humans would agree with me on that one, though. Don’t know why. Just a feeling I have and stuff.)<br><br>④ You know that con about <b>no-burn romances</b>? Guess what? It’s a <b>pro</b>, too. <b>Ha!</b> “Why?” you ask. Because I said so, obviously. And also maybe perhaps because <b>the less <s>lovey dovey crap</s> romance there is in a story</b>, the more my black, withered heart <b>gleefully rejoices</b> and stuff. Ha again!<br><br>⑤ <b>Packs of wolves vs. gaggles of girls</b>. I rest <s>in</s> my case and stuff.<br><br>⑥ <i>“<b>Fucking monkeys</b>. Wither their eyes. Squeeze their hearts into black pulp. <b>Turn them into festering cesspools contained in a weeping bag of skin</b>.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1596454753ra/29909872.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>That’s Gertie the Cheerleading Crab for you. The little darling just can’t help getting her pom poms out of storage and giving them a vigorous workout whenever mass human slaughter is mentioned. Such an enthusiastic little crustacean she is.</i><br><br>➽ <u><b>Nefarious Last Words</b> (NLW™)</u>: <b>7 cons vs. 6 pros</b> and yet I still rated the book <b>4 stars</b>. Goes to show that the minority <b>will kick your ass every single time</b> and stuff. Ha!<br><br><b>P.S.</b> I seem to recall that <i>someone</i> once mentioned that the crap would be <b>severely cut</b> in this review. Looks like <s>someone is full of fish</s> the Others aren’t the only predators with a <b>wonderful sense of humor</b> and stuff. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br>
  <br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1515838847ra/24871802.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>· <b>Book 1</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/955437184" rel="nofollow noopener">Written in Red</a> ★★★★<br>· <b>Book 2</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2208116494" rel="nofollow noopener">Murder of Crows</a> ★★★★<br>· <b>Book 4</b>: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2998185829" rel="nofollow noopener">Marked in Flesh</a> ★★★★<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1554139579i/27300168._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>[<b>Pre-review nonsense</b>]<br><br><b>What the fish is it with this series</b>?! This is yet another installment I should have <b>hated</b> with all the fury of a murderous crustacean on an acid trip! And should have <b>DNFed</b> faster than it takes to say “Fleet Admiral DaShrimp, unleash the shrimps on those puny humans at once!” But I didn't! <b>Ha</b>! I loved every bloody fishing minute of this <b>Lethargically Slow-Paced, Zero-Action Fest of the Many Inconsistencies and Lazy World Building</b> (LSPZAFotMIaLWB™)! <b>Ha again</b>!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592906607ra/29693751.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ <b>Full review to come</b> and stuff.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_991770512" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/991770512" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/991770512?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer991770512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4273604138371987443">I’m sad after finishing <b>Visions of Silver</b> because I truly didn’t want the book to end! I kept thinking “nooooo” as I saw the percentage on my Kindle climbing to 100. I have to say this is my favorite fantasy series out there to date. This installment was very much about Monty and his daughter Lizzy, and the changing relationship between <i>terra indigene</i> and humans. <br/><br/>As we know from the previous books, Elayne, Monty’s former lover, had taken up with Nicolas Scratch, prominent spokesperson of Humans </span>
  <span id="freeText4273604138371987443" style="display:none">I’m sad after finishing <b>Visions of Silver</b> because I truly didn’t want the book to end! I kept thinking “nooooo” as I saw the percentage on my Kindle climbing to 100. I have to say this is my favorite fantasy series out there to date. This installment was very much about Monty and his daughter Lizzy, and the changing relationship between <i>terra indigene</i> and humans. <br /><br />As we know from the previous books, Elayne, Monty’s former lover, had taken up with Nicolas Scratch, prominent spokesperson of Humans First and Last and this becomes very important to the events that play out in Vision in Silver. HFL’s movement stirs up much hate towards the <i>terra indigene</i> and forms a divisive line between the humans who are friendly towards terra indigene and those who are not. <br /><br />The lines between humans and <i>terra indigene</i> in the Lakeside Courtyard, on the other hand, have become blurred. Now instead of thinking of them as just “clever meat”, they’re viewed as members of their human pack, or Meg’s human pack, affording them consideration and protection. These changes in attitude are thanks to Meg, she’s the catalyst, “The Trailblazer” in a new friendship forming between the two kinds. <br /><br />Living outside of an institutionalized situation is also becoming an issue with the rescued Cassandra Sangue girls, as well as Meg. The outside world can easily overwhelm these girls to a dangerous level. <br />But because Meg is a little more self-aware and been on the outside longer, she’s able to recognize triggers that set these girls on edge. <br /><br />There are so many aspects to this series I love to think about, like the “verbal hierarchy” The Others used to indicate the degree of interaction with an individual: they’d use <i>the</i> Lizzy to indicate more of an outsider, or worse <i>that</i> Lizzy to indicate a human they didn’t like. As soon as humans became closer they became just Lizzy or in the case of Meg where there’s special affection and possession assigned, <i>our</i> Meg. The interactions between the humans and <i>terra indigene</i> in the Lakeside Courtyard continue to be fascinating and hilarious at times. <br /><br />Of course the development of the romance between Simon and Meg continues to be my favorite part of the story. Simon and Meg are very new to the dynamics of a romantic relationship (not that they actually know they’re in one) and so some of their feelings take a while click. It’s very entertaining to witness the light coming on. <br /><br />Things are coming to a head with the humans and the <i>terra indigene</i>, especially in regards to the powerful, more dangerous, wild forms of <i>terra indigene</i>. They are for the moment quietly sitting back and watching all the interactions, but could very quickly step in and wipe out all the humans if they become more of a threat. <br /><br />It’s hard to properly express how special and unique this series is. All I can say is if you haven’t picked it up, you are definitely missing out! <br /><i><br />A copy was kindly provided by the publisher via Edelweiss in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br />This review is also posted on <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2015/03/review-vision-in-silver-by-anne-bishop.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4273604138371987443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1547961047" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1547961047" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1547961047?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451465740" href="/book/show/25489473-vision-in-silver">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=fantastic-lit-and-co">fantastic-lit-and-co</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1547961047" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14882916101528453092">Buddy read with- oh, people, you should know it by now. <br/>Buddy read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32524334-nina' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nina</a>, whose <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1548356210?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>review</a> I unremorsefully command you to read. <br/><br/>As a matter of fact, as for <i>Murder of Crows</i> the true rating is <b>3.5</b>, but the general impression that the book left in my impenetrable (especially to myself) mind is closer to four than to three, hence the four stars. <br/>I never said my rating policy was easily understandable. But I can assure you I'm being coherent with myself. <br/><br/><b>"She will show your pups around the Market Sq</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14882916101528453092" style="display:none">Buddy read with- oh, people, you should know it by now. <br />Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/32524334-nina" rel="nofollow noopener">Nina</a>, whose <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1548356210?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">review</a> I unremorsefully command you to read. <br /><br />As a matter of fact, as for <i>Murder of Crows</i> the true rating is <b>3.5</b>, but the general impression that the book left in my impenetrable (especially to myself) mind is closer to four than to three, hence the four stars. <br />I never said my rating policy was easily understandable. But I can assure you I'm being coherent with myself. <br /><br /><b>"She will show your pups around the Market Square,” Simon said.<br />Sarah giggled. Robert said, “We’re not pups; we’re kids.”<br />He eyed Robert and Sarah with more interest. “Little humans can shift into young goats?” </b><br /><br />I want someone to erect a statue in honour of the one and only <b>Simon Wolfgard</b>.<br /><br />•Thing number one to get off my chest: the <b>romance</b>. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No, there is absolutely <b>no progress </b>when it comes to the romance -or better, ther is, but only at the end, and if you want to see it you should arm yourselves with a microscope. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I thought I had to clarify this because I currently find myself in a desperate situation: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I <i>need</i> to know if they get together in book four -yes, yes, <b>I'm looking for a spoiler</b>, you can begin throwing your tomatoes in one, two, three- and not a single one of the lucky souls who have already read it specify that in their reviews. And here I am, like, <i>dying</i>. So this is why I provided this information first giving you the choice whether to get you spoiled or not, and this is why the first thing I'll put in my review of <i>Marked in Flesh</i> when I'll finally read it will be, rigorously under the spoilery tag, if they kiss or not. Stay tuned. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />Now, back to the present.<br />Did I want to punch them in the face? <b>Yes</b>.<br />Did I pray at night for this situation to just get solved? <b>Yes</b>.<br />Did I internally die a little at every page I turned? <b>Yes</b>.<br />Did this influence how much I enjoyed the book? <b>Not in the slightest</b>. Ok, maybe a tiny bit- but only for fangirl-ish reasons, and anyway not enough to call it a decisive factor.<br />The thing is, <b>it makes sense</b>. It's not like the author turned the whole thing in a overly dramatic act or did something as ridiculous as that. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Both Meg and Simon are still too immature to get into a relationship, and, as much as it kills me, I have to acknowledge that if they got together now, their dynamic would have only been awkward and negatively unsecure. I want it to be perfect. If that means more waiting, man, I'll wait. Just please, <b>hurry</b>. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Besides, they are so <b>cute</b>. The circumstances brought me to overly appreciate (and thus squeal in delight for) every littlest thing. It was an odd kind of enjoyment, and <b>I treasured every moment</b>.<br /><br />•<b>Plot-wise</b>, <i>Vision in Silver</i> was so much better than <i>Murder of Crows</i>, almost at the level of <i>Written in Red</i>, I daresay. Which, by the way, I feel the urge to reread. <br />Anyway, in a few words, I think that what makes this plot truly captivating is that finally the world beyond the Courtyard comes more into play. Not only, but, basically, the central part of <b>the action takes place there, on the outside</b>, and though we don't get to see it directly, everything is reported by way of a couple of dirrent <b>narrative -and stylistic- choices</b> that, in addition, lent the narration a peculiar<b> sense of perspective</b> that proves to be <b>higly intriguing</b>: the reader feels trapped (I'm not using this term in any negative sense) in the Courtyard, and yet the mystery to solve is located on the outside. I came to think of it as of the opposite of a locked-room mystery. Really enjoyable.<br /><br />•But now there comes a <b>touchy subject</b>: <b>Meg</b>. If you read my previous reviews for this series, you know how much I loved her character. A curious mixture of shyness and fierceness, innocence and hunger. Well, here, in the first dozen of chapters or so, Meg experiences an <b>inexplicable regression</b> that stunned, angered and outraged me. I sincerely don't know where it came from or how it was even possible. One moment she was just fine- the next she was wailing like a baby because she noticed she's having troubles adapting to the world outside the compund. <br />I could have accepted that if she <b>hadn't handled everything just fine for the previous four</b> -or whatever-<b> months</b>.<br />I understand that the autor needed a way to give her the means and a contingency to write the Guide, but <b>at the expense of the protagonist's characterization</b>? My answer would have been a ginormous <i>No, thank you</i>.<br /><br />•As a proof that Bishop had just had a moment of perdition -only Namid knows why- and that she has not lost her touch, <b>all the other characters</b> are simply as <b>fantastic</b> as they were in the previous books, and, to be fair, after those first chapters Meg even gets back to her old self, for the joy of everyone. Moreover, Monty and her daughter are really sweet, and Elayne's character, who before had so little relevance, no only becomes crucial, but also shows some shades of herself that actually moved me.<br /><br />In a nutshell, I appreciated and enjoyed this book for a couple of reasond that are surely different from the ones for which I enjoyed Murder of Crows and only partially identifiable in the ones for which I enjoyed Written in Red.<b> It lacked some things, but was nonetheless full of surprises</b>.<br /><br />Now give me <i>Marked in Flesh</i>. I'll give you a Wolf cookie. And another quote:<br /><br /><b>"Why do a field trip?"<br />"Because someone untied its shoes?"<br />Meg frowned. "That makes no sense."</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14882916101528453092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1394606492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1394606492" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1394606492?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=werewolves-and-other-furry-shifters">werewolves-and-other-furry-shifters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1394606492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3368219899907922912"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442554173ra/16251761.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Now that I am finished with this book, I have to wait an entire year for the next one. And, I just can't do that. Nope. Not good at waiting. At all.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442554173ra/16251762.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I love this series so much! There is no end to the amazing characters who are so well written that they steal my heart. I just want Anne Bishop locked in a room, writing, forever, so that I can keep reading her books. Is that too much to ask?<br/><br/>So, in this book, we are really continuing on with the story that has been shaping up for a while. There is a </span>
  <span id="freeText3368219899907922912" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442554173ra/16251761.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now that I am finished with this book, I have to wait an entire year for the next one. And, I just can't do that. Nope. Not good at waiting. At all.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442554173ra/16251762.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love this series so much! There is no end to the amazing characters who are so well written that they steal my heart. I just want Anne Bishop locked in a room, writing, forever, so that I can keep reading her books. Is that too much to ask?<br><br>So, in this book, we are really continuing on with the story that has been shaping up for a while. There is a hate-group out there called "Humans First and Last" that is trying to drum up trouble for the Others. They have an evil spokesman and everything. Like most hate groups, they have more hot air than sense. You know, considering that the Others can just decide to kill all of the humans in just a day and be done with it. But, nooo, they are going to keep poking the bear. Literally.<br><br>Simon, the wolf, is trying to keep Meg happy by keeping her "Human pack" safe when the hate-group starts targeting all "wolf-lovers". It's getting ugly in the human world so keeping some of them safe is getting difficult.<br><br>In the meantime, Monty, the cop, finally gets his daughter to come and live with him. But, along with her comes a whole lot of trouble because her mother was with the evil spokesman for the hate-group, and they killed her. Now, they are targeting the little girl because she may have some evidence of what happened.<br><br>All of this makes Simon consider ways to keep the wolf-lover humans safe by having them live among the Others. Since this has never been done, it makes for a lot of adjustments. Especially since the Others have so little understanding of humans. Of course, I love that part of the book the most because the misunderstandings are funny.<br><br>When Simon called some kids "pups":<br><b>
  <i>Sarah giggled. Robert said, "We're not pups; we're kids."<br>He eyed Robert and Sarah with more interest. "Little humans can shift into young goats?"</i>
</b><br><br>When Vlad, the vampire, wanted some human women to leave his office:<br><b>
  <i>He picked up a pen and moved a couple of papers on the desk. He'd seen a human in a movie do that as a way to end a meeting. Apparently, the females hadn't seen the movie.</i>
</b><br><br>I also loved the way all of the Others acted like the teddy bear was alive, or had feelings. It was so freaking cute and funny.<br><br>When Lizzy was talking to the police and said that Boo Bear might have been to blame for the bad-guys following her:<br><b>
  <i>Nathan considered this information...It sounded like human young didn't know enough to stay quiet and hidden when a predator came sniffing around the den. Didn't seem fair to blame Boo Bear, though, since he wouldn't have blabbed to anyone.</i>
</b><br><br>So many times, when I was reading the different wolves thoughts while they were trying to understand the humans, I thought of my dogs when they do that cute head-tilt thing. You know, when they act like they are trying to understand you?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1442554173ra/16251763.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Aww, that's so cute. Let's give him something!</i><br><br>But, most of all, I love the relationship between Meg and Simon. Since Meg doesn't know how to human any better than Simon does, it is super adorable watching them grow into a romance of sorts. There has been no actual romance in the books at all, but it seems like it may be heading that way. Very very slowly. I am dying for Simon and Meg to get together. They will be the cutest couple ever!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3368219899907922912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4561998-carmel-rabid-reads?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer918309383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7651633589820525604"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/03/early-review-vision-in-silver-by-anne-bishop.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a>.</b><br/><br/>Let it be known that this series is peerless; Anne Bishop’s world-building is innovative, her characters are exceptional, and the story is obsession inducing. I picked-up WRITTEN IN RED on a whim in 2013, and was wowed beyond measure. My fixation with all things THE OTHERS is so profound that it should be a bona fide medical condition. No joke! I listened to the previous two installments, so I did have some concerns that switching to hard copy might diminish my enjoyment</span>
  <span id="freeText7651633589820525604" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/03/early-review-vision-in-silver-by-anne-bishop.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a>.</b><br /><br />Let it be known that this series is peerless; Anne Bishop’s world-building is innovative, her characters are exceptional, and the story is obsession inducing. I picked-up WRITTEN IN RED on a whim in 2013, and was wowed beyond measure. My fixation with all things THE OTHERS is so profound that it should be a bona fide medical condition. No joke! I listened to the previous two installments, so I did have some concerns that switching to hard copy might diminish my enjoyment of VISION IN SILVER, but that clearly didn’t happen because for the third time in a row 5-stars just isn’t enough. In this book we learn a lot more about the cassandra sangue, gain perspective on Simon Wolfgard, and get a glimpse of the terra indigene that live beyond the courtyards.<br /><br />The blood prophets were the main plot focal point; free of their keepers, these girls are ill-equipped for life outside the compounds, and now it’s up to Meg to set them on the correct path. She and the other members of her human pack are attempting to write a sweet blood 101 guide of sorts. Little is known about the cassandra sangue, so a lot of it came down to trial &amp; error with Corbyn as the lab rat. I liked how the author approached this aspect of the story, the progression was gradual, and each new discovery felt as though it could be the key to their very survival. Meg’s triumphs became mine, and her setbacks were absolutely devastating. Most were small things, but when experienced from such an innocent POV as this series’ protagonist, they became monumental.<br /><br />Most stories that feature shifters put emphasis on the humanness of the characters while as Bishop does the total opposite. Her various gards don people flesh out of necessity, but it’s evident that they prefer fur, and view mankind as ‘clever meat.’ This is part of what makes THE OTHERS universe so original because misunderstandings between the two species occur frequently from common expressions being taken literally to every day gestures being grossly misinterpreted. I enjoyed gaining perspective on how the terra indigene see the world through Simon because he’s the most progressive leader among them which makes his outlook fabulously unique. He’s tasked with a huge decision at the end of this novel, and the outcome could be… scary.<br /><br />This leads me to this book’s second main plot thread. Tension between THE OTHERS and humans has reached a boiling point, the Humans First and Last movement is gaining momentum and people are being forced to choose a side. You’re either a Wolf lover or a delusional HFL supporter who believes that mankind actually has a chance at being the dominant species. Bishop has succeeded in making me hate my own kind by illustrating the barbaric nature of Thaisia’s citizens, and highlighting the underlying prejudice that exists in all societies. The author makes it impossible not to cheer for the terra indigene, and eagerly anticipate the fast approaching day of reckoning when the wild country finally shows its teeth, and establishes once and for all who’s predator and who’s prey.<br /><br />There’s only one cure for a VISION IN SILVER book hangover, and it’s more Meg &amp; Simon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7651633589820525604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3788551888590626631">I hate to say it but this instalment in the series was boring. The book started off promising with the conflict between the humans and terra indigene but this plot overpowered everything else in the book. There was little to no character growth between Meg and the inhabitants of the courtyard. This was particularly annoying in relation to Meg and Simon. Everyone, including readers and the characters in the book, know where this relationship is going and yet nothing has happened to further my int</span>
  <span id="freeText3788551888590626631" style="display:none">I hate to say it but this instalment in the series was boring. The book started off promising with the conflict between the humans and terra indigene but this plot overpowered everything else in the book. There was little to no character growth between Meg and the inhabitants of the courtyard. This was particularly annoying in relation to Meg and Simon. Everyone, including readers and the characters in the book, know where this relationship is going and yet nothing has happened to further my interest in this relationship. The most growth that happened between these two happened in the first book. I would have been okay with this if the plot was intriguing but I found myself constantly skipping through pages since I was bored. This book did not ignite the need in me to immediately know what happens next like the first book did and I'm unsure if I will continue on with this series. <br /><br />*ARC provided by NetGalley. </span>

<div id="review_2183679681" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2183679681" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2183679681?book_show_action=true">Nov 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bb-b-2017">bb-b-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=uf-pnr">uf-pnr</a>
