        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2183679681" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12252310891483143934">I want to preface this by saying I totally enjoy this series. <br/><br/>I like Meg. I like Simon. I’m keep hoping that somehow they will hook up and soon but it is really slow on that front….like snail pace slow. Still even though the romance I long for is waiting to catch fire that didn’t diminish my enjoyment of this book.<br/><br/>There are a few issues though that I saw in this. It sometimes gets a bit repetitive. Good if you are going a year between books and need a refresher, everything from prior books is br</span>
  <span id="freeText12252310891483143934" style="display:none">I want to preface this by saying I totally enjoy this series. <br /><br />I like Meg. I like Simon. I’m keep hoping that somehow they will hook up and soon but it is really slow on that front….like snail pace slow. Still even though the romance I long for is waiting to catch fire that didn’t diminish my enjoyment of this book.<br /><br />There are a few issues though that I saw in this. It sometimes gets a bit repetitive. Good if you are going a year between books and need a refresher, everything from prior books is brought up and distilled down. But if you are reading these back to back then I think it might be an issue.<br /><br />The other issue I had was actually with Meg’s character. In the last two books she is fragile and strong all at the same time. Her fragility has more to do with the world around her and being really sensitive to her surroundings. But now she is having panic attack like symptoms. Yes this plays into the overall plot with the other blood prophets who aren’t in captivity anymore but it was a little bit of a stretch. That said though I liked that with her human girl pack they are working to discover some of the mysteries of the blood prophets to share with others.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“What do you expect us to do?” Meg shouted. “Write The Dimwit’s Guide to Blood Prophets?” <br />“Yes! That’s exactly what I want you to do.” <br />Looking at their stunned expressions, he wondered if he’d been a little too honest. “Figure it out and write it up so we can pass on the information to everyone who is trying to help these girls.” <br />“I’m not a writer,” Merri Lee protested. “I can make notes, sure, but I can’t write up something like that!” <br />“Ruthie will help you write it.” There. Problem solved. Ruthie was a teacher. She wrote sentences all the time.</i>
</blockquote><br />But the story is still good and I like the addition of both Jean and Hope in their communities. This is one of those books that makes me hate humans. Yes not all are bad but it does speak to what happens when one group thinks they are more important than all the others and decide to get mean about it.<br /><blockquote>
  <i> Didn’t humans realize the terra indigene had heard such words before? Didn’t humans understand that such words were a warning that a fight for territory was building under the surface? Didn’t they wonder what had happened to cities, and civilizations, the previous times humans had made such claims?</i>
</blockquote><br />I still love seeing the world through the Others eyes and finding how different they think from us. I mean just buying a building can be a little bit hilarious.<br /><blockquote>
  <i> Why couldn’t they just give the human female a bag of money and then pee on the building so that everyone would know it was theirs?</i>
</blockquote><br />The violence between the factions is escalating and soon there will be no going back for sure. Especially the lengths the Humans First and Last movement is getting. I’m both excited and terrified to see what lives in the deep wild and is a protector of the land. <br /><br />There are a few heartbreaking moments and more development on the Cel Remano story arc and just what Nicolas Scratch is planning. Plus finally we get to meet Lizzy and he furry bear companion. I think it was adorable to see some human children enter the Pack’s life. There in for some surprises.<br /><br />Overall I’m still very much enjoying the different take on shifters and this UF world. I do wish we could speed up the Simon/Meg romance but other than that I’m just going to enjoy the rollout of the rest of the story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12252310891483143934" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/993229453?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steven" href="/user/show/11855472-steven">Steven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11855472-steven?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11855472-steven?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer993229453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11353366722722183186">This series is quickly becoming one of my top favorites. Such an interesting world. I'm totally caught up in the lives and challenges of these two groups of people struggling to make things work in a world that is headed towards a war. The Others and their "human pack" are such an intriguing story to read. I love the growth we've seen in the Others as they come to care for some humans, and the increase in number of humans on the "right side of history." <br/><br/>This book was darker than the previous two</span>
  <span id="freeText11353366722722183186" style="display:none">This series is quickly becoming one of my top favorites. Such an interesting world. I'm totally caught up in the lives and challenges of these two groups of people struggling to make things work in a world that is headed towards a war. The Others and their "human pack" are such an intriguing story to read. I love the growth we've seen in the Others as they come to care for some humans, and the increase in number of humans on the "right side of history." <br /><br />This book was darker than the previous two. We lost a few good characters in it and it seriously broke my heart. <br /><br />I see Hope in the darkness. The darkness is growing stronger and deeper, but there is a light there waiting to help overcome it.<br /><br />I can't help but feel that by the end, Meg will be the required sacrifice for a world at peace. I hope not, but I feel like Anne Bishop is preparing us for that potential. <br /><br />And so begins the wait for book four. Two books remain in the series, if I remember correctly. I'm ready for the next chapter!</span>

<div id="review_2190991942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2190991942" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2190991942?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2190991942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6972508502622270673"><b>*** 4.44 ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with my family at the Wednesday BB&B Urban Fantasy Group! </b><br/><br/>This series continues to get better and better. The overall arc of humans trying to live in harmony with the original inhabitants of the planet, The Others, and failing miserably, has taken a very interesting route under the treatment of the author, Anne Bishop. I have heard many times that you either like her writing or you hate it, and once again I am finding out that I am on "I Love It" side of the argument. Is</span>
  <span id="freeText6972508502622270673" style="display:none"><b>*** 4.44 ***<br /><br />A buddy read with my family at the Wednesday BB&amp;B Urban Fantasy Group! </b><br /><br />This series continues to get better and better. The overall arc of humans trying to live in harmony with the original inhabitants of the planet, The Others, and failing miserably, has taken a very interesting route under the treatment of the author, Anne Bishop. I have heard many times that you either like her writing or you hate it, and once again I am finding out that I am on "I Love It" side of the argument. Is there a particular reason for that? No, not really. There is something about her storytelling though, that speaks to my love for small details, which enrich the big picture, even when those small details seem silly or superfluous... For me they add this charm and whimsical feeling to a story, which at times might seems as if it is stalling, but instead it just builds on the emotional connection of the reader with the world and characters. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"...“For now, he and Meg were going to have the adventure of seeing a new place and having a new experience. Together.<br />He wasn't human. Would never be human. And Meg didn't expect him to be. But feeling her hand in his, Simon thought maybe he could learn to be human enough.” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Once again, the romance that all of us saw coming from the first chapter of the first book, between the very wolfy-wolf Simon and the very sheltered and innocent Blood-Prophet Meg, did not reach even to a kiss, although I think they are considering some hand-holding:) And this is perfectly fine with me:) I love the way the two of them, just as the two cultural groups they represent, are finding out more about each-other, discovering things necessary for their shared safety, but also things that just make you smile... And as raw and animalistic as the Others are, and as much as they have looked upon humans as "Smart Meat", there are breakthroughs happening in the human-Others relationships, mostly because of the budding romance between Simon and Meg, and also all species of Others in the Lakeside Courtyard and Meg, whose visions have kept them safe more than once already. It just sucks for all of them that this is the time the "Humans First and Last" or HFL movement has decided to incite violence between the two groups in order to make money off of Humanity's suffering and blame it on the Others, thus starting a civil war... Humans blame The Others for everything that befalls them, attack and when there are consequences, they blame The Others once again, unwilling to admit or even see that they are the true culprits... No wonder some of the Big-Bad Others, who don't even come in contact with the humans, are fed up and thinking about Exterminating the species from the continent... And I have to agree, the Humans kind of deserve it... <br /><br />As bad as it is on the Big Scale of things, the Courtyard residents are falling in love with their Meg, who is trying to figure out ways to help the newly freed Blood-Prophet girls in order to stay alive... Freedom seams to be very difficult for them, since a strict sensory input control has to be imposed, but most who have taken the girls in with the desire to help are fully unqualified to do so, not having any idea of how to even approach what the real issues are... Meg feels safe in her own circle of friends and those whom she consideres family now - Simon and Sam, as well as the newly forming Human Pack. Favorite part of the whole book was when the mother of two human children told him that they are not called pups, but kids...<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"..."...Sarah giggled. Robert said, “We’re not pups; we’re kids.”<br />Simon looked at Robert and Sarah, then at Ruthie.<br />Kids. He’d heard Merri Lee say something about when she was a kid. But the word didn’t apply to her now because she was an adult, so it had never occurred to him that, maybe, humans had a little shifter ability that they outgrew as they matured. When she had said kid, maybe she had meant kid?<br />He eyed Robert and Sarah with more interest. “Little humans can shift into young goats?” Kids were tasty. Would human-turned-goat taste different from goat-goat?” ..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Hahahaha!!!! I guess we do change forms from when we are kids to adults:) Magic!!! <br /><br />Still, my favorite characters were scary Tess and the developmentally disabled pup, Skippy! I want them to adopt me into their pack!!!<br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and many more wonderful books to come!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6972508502622270673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5375148-beth?shelf=dark">dark</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5375148-beth?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1162295589" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11474409315577152092"><i>Vision in Silver</i> is an utterly brilliant addition to The Other Series by Anne Bishop.<br/><br/>Simon Wolfgard, leader of the Courtyard, is dealing with the aftermath of <i>cassandra sangue's</i> freedom. The once exploited seers are not handling their new freedom very well. There are those who wish to use the difficulties to regaining use of <i>cassandra sangue</i> while causing political turmoil against the Others. <br/><br/>Someone is trying to insight war between the inhabitants of Atlantik. The treachery is growing in the hu</span>
  <span id="freeText11474409315577152092" style="display:none"><i>Vision in Silver</i> is an utterly brilliant addition to The Other Series by Anne Bishop.<br><br>Simon Wolfgard, leader of the Courtyard, is dealing with the aftermath of <i>cassandra sangue's</i> freedom. The once exploited seers are not handling their new freedom very well. There are those who wish to use the difficulties to regaining use of <i>cassandra sangue</i> while causing political turmoil against the Others. <br><br>Someone is trying to insight war between the inhabitants of Atlantik. The treachery is growing in the human government, hopefully they realize they live by the Others' leave before its too late.<br><br>In the Courtyard, the bond between humans, <i>cassandra sanque</i> and the Others is evolving. It is truly amazing. Meg is also struggling with her urges. With the help of the Courtyard residents, she is discovering ways to help herself and her fellow <i>cassandra sanque</i>. <br><br>Anne Bishop pulls you into this world she created and happily holds you riveted to every single word she’s written. Not only does Bishop bring the conflict between the Others and humans to the forefront but also captures the turmoil its causes within the individual groups; the divides it creates in families, work place and society’s core. <br><br>Bishop captures the essence of humanity at its worst and best and infuses it into her characters.<br><br>This series might be the most unique, captivating and utterly brilliant Dark Urban Fantasy I’ve ever read. Truly hitting the top of all my favorites! I flat out loved this book and this entire series. <br><br><i>Vision in Silver</i> has completely rocked me, jarred my emotions and kept me clinging to the pages. <br><br><i>Vision in Silver</i> is dark at times and can be quite distressing so it is not for those who prefer meeker reads. <br><br>I would highly recommend this book and series; especially those who enjoy complex urban fantasy reads. Today, March 3, 2015 is release day GO BUY IT TODAY!<br><br>I received this ARC copy of <i>Vision in Silver</i> from Roc in exchange for a honest review. This book is set for publication March 3, 2015.<br><br><a href="http://s1342.photobucket.com/user/bethh77/media/0004_zps4c7ee41a.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt=" photo 0004_zps4c7ee41a.gif" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380414662ra/817652.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1225827504">
  <td colspan="2">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer912529169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14239825217539480116"><b>This series is pure comfort reading for me now.</b> I can't explain why but even when the characters are planting a garden I'm engaged. And when Tess gets mad I need to know <i>why</i> and what exactly is a "picnic that's not a picnic" and who is this new person and what is the plan and why are ...<br/><br/>Just neverending questions and WHAT HAPPENS NEXT. I <b>need</b> to read about these characters' lives and how things are changing for them: it's no longer just a <i>want</i>. And I swear that almost every time Meg tears up I d</span>
  <span id="freeText14239825217539480116" style="display:none"><b>This series is pure comfort reading for me now.</b> I can't explain why but even when the characters are planting a garden I'm engaged. And when Tess gets mad I need to know <i>why</i> and what exactly is a "picnic that's not a picnic" and who is this new person and what is the plan and why are ...<br /><br />Just neverending questions and WHAT HAPPENS NEXT. I <b>need</b> to read about these characters' lives and how things are changing for them: it's no longer just a <i>want</i>. And I swear that almost every time Meg tears up I did too. I don't know what it is about her finding out new things that's so endearing but I'm right there with her. Also, the way the wolves think and act are so NOT human that I'm really starting to wonder if the author ... moonlights.<br /><br /><b>This is urban fantasy and not paranormal romance so don't go in thinking there's going to be any romance of the sort.</b> But. There's something I tend to like more, even though it's taking a very, very, VERY long time to develop. These are Others who barely even <i>tolerated</i> humans but now guard and interact with Meg like she belongs so I can understand how any sort of love or romance would take a while to manifest. It's definitely there though and I can't wait to see what happens with THAT.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1204185933" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204185933" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14323468-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434090906p2/14323468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1204185933?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/14323468-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780451465740" href="/book/show/25489473-vision-in-silver">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone who loves Urban Fantasy!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=mine">mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=book-boyfriend">book-boyfriend</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=gr2017">gr2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=books-i-love">books-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204185933" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2353788838724610809"><blockquote>
  <i>She wasn’t a Wolf. She wasn’t terra indigene. Despite that, Meg was becoming one of them.</i>
</blockquote> <p>There are no words to convey how much I LOVE this series!!!</p> <p>
  <u>SPOILERS AHEAD FOR THE PREVIOUS BOOKS.</u>
</p> <p>When the Others saved the cassandra sangue from their jailers, they never expected the danger that would follow. No one knows how to protect these fragile seers, especially when all of them seems unable to handle their new surroundings. And the only one who can provide the answers to saving them is Meg</p></span>
  <span id="freeText2353788838724610809" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>She wasn’t a Wolf. She wasn’t terra indigene. Despite that, Meg was becoming one of them.</i>
</blockquote> <p>There are no words to convey how much I LOVE this series!!!</p> <p>
  <u>SPOILERS AHEAD FOR THE PREVIOUS BOOKS.</u>
</p> <p>When the Others saved the cassandra sangue from their jailers, they never expected the danger that would follow. No one knows how to protect these fragile seers, especially when all of them seems unable to handle their new surroundings. And the only one who can provide the answers to saving them is Meg Corbyn. Simon Wolfgard hates asking Meg for help in saving the blood prophets, knowing she would have to face risks in order to do so, but he has no choice, she’s their only hope. </p> <p>When blood prophets start to only predict devastation and death, it seems to be a warning of things to come. The HFL, humans first and last, movement is becoming stronger, gaining more human followers and posing a big threat to the Others and to those who interact with them. They don’t care to what lengths they need to go to spread their prejudice, the betrayals they need to commit to win their fight. </p> <p>Meg is still a wonderful complex character. She’s still struggling with her addiction to cutting and it makes her friends very worried about her. But even though she knows that her kind can only survive a thousand cuts, her fear about missing some valuable clues that could save her friends, makes it hard for her to resist. I couldn’t blame Meg for needing to know about the dangers they would face, but seeing how addicted she was to cutting made panic. Is she ever going to be able to grow old??? The only thing that bothered me a bit about her in this book was her sudden inability to cope with her surroundings, with any changes. I guess it was necessary so that she could help the other blood prophets navigate their issues with adapting, but the sudden change did confuse me a bit. </p> <p>The plot continues to escalate with the HFL making things worse for the Others and their friends and acquaintances, and it definitely seems that a war is coming. And I for one can’t wait to see these monstrous HFLs get eaten. </p> <p>As always I loved spending time with all the characters and I’ve come to love all of them. I love how attached the Others has become to Meg and her human pack, especially since there has never been any kind of bond like this before between the two different species in this world. I also really like that we’re getting to know more of the other blood prophets, and seeing what they are capable of. </p> <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>He wasn’t human. Would never be human. And Meg didn’t expect him to be. But feeling her hand in his, Simon thought maybe he could learn to be human enough.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote> <p>The <i>very</i> slow romance between Meg and Simon keeps making my heart melt. I love how much their friendship means to them, and how possessive Simon is becoming of Meg. They are definitely one of my favorite couples ever, and they’re not even a couple yet!! :-D </p> <p>I adore this series and I just want to inhale every page!! Anne Bishop has created a unique and fascinating world, with amazing characters and plot. <b>HIGHLY RECOMMENDED TO ALL UF FANS!!!.</b> </p></span>
  <a data-text-id="2353788838724610809" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_985588648" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/985588648" />
    <a title="Kathe L" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25921490-kathe-l"><img alt="Kathe L" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421550107p2/25921490.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/985588648?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathe L" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathe L" href="/user/show/25921490-kathe-l">Kathe L</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=didn-t-expect-to-be-so-good">didn-t-expect-to-be-so-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=fav-female-characters">fav-female-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=bad-boy-i-love-you">bad-boy-i-love-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25921490-kathe-l?shelf=look-there-s-a-werewolf">look-there-s-a-werewolf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer985588648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5837997873174485880">The first half of this book is like a gigantic <i>puzzle.</i> It gives you tons of information and builds a world and situations that are bond to happen. You know it. The thing is: sometimes, you don't understand why what you are reading is so important. <b>But it is.</b> And it will come back later and you'll be 'ahhh now it makes sense.'<br/><br/><b>"She wasn't a wolf. She wasn't a terra indigene. Despite that, Meg was becoming one of them."</b> <br/><br/>While Meg, the blood prophet who has to cut herself in order to have visions of</span>
  <span id="freeText5837997873174485880" style="display:none">The first half of this book is like a gigantic <i>puzzle.</i> It gives you tons of information and builds a world and situations that are bond to happen. You know it. The thing is: sometimes, you don't understand why what you are reading is so important. <b>But it is.</b> And it will come back later and you'll be 'ahhh now it makes sense.'<br><br><b>"She wasn't a wolf. She wasn't a terra indigene. Despite that, Meg was becoming one of them."</b> <br><br>While Meg, the blood prophet who has to cut herself in order to have visions of the future, isn't as present in the first half as I'd have liked to, she is there in the second one and she <i>grew</i> so much! In this book, Meg realized that for the first time in her life the terra indigene are her friends and love her for who she is, not because she can save them through her visions. In fact, they don't want her to cut because they want her to live with them as long as possible. And Simon, Meg's best friend (and hopefully lover in the future *crossed fingers*), cares for her so deeply that their scenes are always what I look forward the most. <br><br><b>"Feeling her hand in his, Simon thought maybe he could learn to be human enough."</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426023076i/13963926.jpg" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Simon, the great leader and a wolf, is very present in this book and I was so happy! While in the first book I thought he was very narrow-minded and got angry too fast, he grew on me in a way I've never seen before. In the last book and in this book, I was always very anxious to hear his sides of the story and was very happy when it was his POV. He always had thoughts of Meg that weren't hard to hear. (Who am I kidding? I <i>live</i> for Meg and Simon.) He has to deal with a lot in this book because he and the others/terra indigenes (wolfs, vampires, bears, Elementals, crows, you name it) have to face humans and all the wrong accusations they make of the Terra Indigene every day. <b>This book is practically all focused on the relationship between our paranormal group and humans.</b> I have no shame in saying that I will always root for the others - in this book, I was ashamed of our race but proud of Montgomery, Meg, even Merry Lee. (Humans who think in this series.) <br><br><b>-It feels different, this scar. <br>- It's a sign of a caring heart. It should feel different. <br>- We take care of each other, don't we? <br>- Yes, we do.</b> <br><br>(The relationship between Meg and the others &lt;3) This book made me nervous. It made me read it so fast I only realized I had reached the middle of it because my brother said I wasn't even blinking and when I did, I saw the page I was in. I waited <i>so long</i> for this book and I'm almost kicking myself for reading it so fast. Everyone grew, and I was a very proud mom. These books are not for everyone, in fact, they are not my typical kind of book, either. But once I fell in love with the environment, the characters, the mystery, the situations they have faced and will have to face yet in the future, I couldn't be happier for giving this series a shot. <br><br>It is funny? Yes, because the others often wonder about human things and I always find myself <i>giggling.</i> The romance? You will never root <b>so much</b> for characters that are soooo slow. It has mind blowing situations and this book even had a bit of politics, something I always thought as boring but that in this book made me feel as if I was in the middle of a chess game or in a game of 'war'. Seriously, I can talk all day long about this series and never be bored. <br><br>Blood prophets are shown on this one, corrupt governments, the 'wild side', and our lovely characters are as present as ever. Tess, I love you. You're bad-ass. Vlad, you're the sexiest vampire. Henry, I want to hug you and never let you go. Simon, *sigh*. Jenny, I felt your pain! And Nathan, come be my wolf guard, would you? All Bella (my Yorkshire) does is sleep. <br><br>What to do now? Die waiting for the next one (and it has to have another one, otherwise I'll die for sure.) Read this series people! the first book will pull you in this fantastic series and you'll find yourself hypnotized by the story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5837997873174485880" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1184295599" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1184295599" />
    <a title="Paranormal Kiss" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4047913-paranormal-kiss"><img alt="Paranormal Kiss" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294530519p2/4047913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1184295599?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paranormal Kiss" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paranormal Kiss" href="/user/show/4047913-paranormal-kiss">Paranormal Kiss</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22456990-vision-in-silver">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4047913-paranormal-kiss?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4047913-paranormal-kiss?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4047913-paranormal-kiss?shelf=free-review-copy">free-review-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4047913-paranormal-kiss?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4047913-paranormal-kiss?shelf=sci-fi-and-fantasy">sci-fi-and-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1184295599" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7807744333798126584">Vision in Silver is the 3rd book in The Others series by Anne Bishop. I liked this one but compared to the first two books it was a bit of a letdown. In this book, the story is told from the viewpoints of several characters. While in the first two books we read from mainly Meg’s perspective. I adored her voice. Unfortunately we don’t get nearly as much from Meg in this one. <br/><br/>I’ve never been a fan of reading books that are told from a large cast of characters, as this one was. The perspective is s</span>
  <span id="freeText7807744333798126584" style="display:none">Vision in Silver is the 3rd book in The Others series by Anne Bishop. I liked this one but compared to the first two books it was a bit of a letdown. In this book, the story is told from the viewpoints of several characters. While in the first two books we read from mainly Meg’s perspective. I adored her voice. Unfortunately we don’t get nearly as much from Meg in this one. <br /><br />I’ve never been a fan of reading books that are told from a large cast of characters, as this one was. The perspective is so much broader and less focused on personal development. Because of that, I really didn’t connect with some of the characters, particularly Burke and Monty. Additionally, the different storylines need to be equally interesting. Otherwise, I find myself wanting to rush through the less interesting parts and back to the interesting ones, as I did with this novel. <br /><br />Another thing that bothered me is that it got bogged down, at times, with too much information. Honestly, parts of the story were downright boring. There just wasn’t a lot of progress. There was a lot of buildup and then it just tapers off to a conclusion that was rather sedate. It almost felt like running in place. <br /><br />That’s not to say that Vision in Silver didn’t have some good parts, it did. Tensions are rising with the HFL, Humans First and Last, movement, as they step up their plot to turn humans against The Others. Little do they realize how incredibly stupid their aggressive and prejudice actions against The Others is. And those actions aren’t without serious consequence. <br /><br />In Vision in Silver, Simon takes steps to further integrate with humans. I enjoyed getting a deeper insight into his character and his view of things. We see the strong bond between him and Meg. She is his friend, one of the most important people in his life. Because of her, he has completely changed how he views humans. She is the reason for all the changes in the Courtyard. Their dynamic is interesting and entertaining. Actually, the whole Courtyard dynamic is fascinating and I like seeing how the characters cope with the changes taking place and learning more about them. I also enjoyed reading about one of the girls that was rescued in the last book and seeing her progress.<br /><br />In conclusion, Vision in Silver is a good book. I just didn’t find it to be a compelling or fascinating read. I liked it but I was expecting more. I can only hope the next one is better.<br /><br />To see more of my reviews go to <a href="https://paranormalkiss.wixsite.com/paranormalkiss/single-post/Vision-in-Silver-by-Anne-Bishop" rel="nofollow noopener">Paranormal Kiss</a>.<br /><br /><i>*ARC (Advanced Review Copy) received from the publisher, PENGUIN GROUP/Roc, via NetGalley.</i></span>

<div id="review_1098467029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1098467029" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1098467029?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1098467029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer520556367705196401">The Meg is back! Well, she is not actually The Meg anymore. She's Our Meg and that may be even better.<br/><br/>If you have no idea what I am talking about, you are clearly missing out on one of my favorite Urban Fantasy series and you need to stop what you are doing and go buy <i>Written in Red</i>. No really. Do it now.<br/><br/>This third installment picks up right on the heels of book 2. It follows Meg as she continues to find balance, free of the Controller and the Walking Names who shaped her life for so long. She h</span>
  <span id="freeText520556367705196401" style="display:none">The Meg is back! Well, she is not actually The Meg anymore. She's Our Meg and that may be even better.<br /><br />If you have no idea what I am talking about, you are clearly missing out on one of my favorite Urban Fantasy series and you need to stop what you are doing and go buy <i>Written in Red</i>. No really. Do it now.<br /><br />This third installment picks up right on the heels of book 2. It follows Meg as she continues to find balance, free of the Controller and the Walking Names who shaped her life for so long. She has come a long way, but she still struggles with her need to cut. Now it's not just her life on the line, but the lives of all the girls rescued who are like her. Meg needs to understand herself and her triggers in order to help those like her survive in the outside world.<br /><br />Meanwhile, tension is nearing the breaking point between humans and the Others. Right in the middle of it all are Monty and his little girl, Lizzie. We've heard from the beginning how hard it has been for him to be apart from her. Now, circumstances are reuniting them, but at what cost? There are humans vying for supremacy and making the very big mistake of forgetting who the real dominant species is on Earth. It's a powder keg just waiting to blow.<br /><br />There are so many things I like about these books. The world-building is fantastic. Yes, there is a glossary and some made up words, but it's nothing that is going to make you feel lost. In fact, it's really very easy to fall into this world without having to give it much thought at all. I also really love the Others of the Lakeside Courtyard. Simon, of course, is my favorite, but I'll get back to him in a minute. Tess is such a fantastic secondary character. I also love Nathan, Henry, and Sam. It's fascinating watching how they interact with Meg... how they are evolving. They are monsters, no doubt, but the deeper we get into these books, we see how much more monstrous humans can be. Ooooh. And they are gonna get theirs.<br /><br />My only small niggle: I am ready to move a little bit further in the relationship between Simon and Meg. I know this is not a romance and I understand why they're not doing the dirty in one of the upstairs rooms. But Anne Bishop keeps dropping all of these little hints that something is happening there. For three books, <i>something</i> has been happening. The thing is, I need a little <i>more</i> something. When it takes three months to culminate in holding a hand, well, we might could pick up the pace just a bit.<br /><br />I didn't find this installment quite as strong as the first two. Overall, though, this remains a consistently fantastic series. It's entertaining, easy reading, and still thought provoking. Would definitely recommend.<br /><br />Rating: B+<br /><br /><i>*ARC provided by publisher</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="520556367705196401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_886667821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/886667821" />
    <a title="Lila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6659789-lila"><img alt="Lila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426228692p2/6659789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/886667821?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lila" href="/user/show/6659789-lila">Lila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6659789-lila?shelf=2015-dhasg-challenge">2015-dhasg-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6659789-lila?shelf=uf">uf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer886667821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14304273570674307329">3,5 stars<br/><br/> With unlike heroine, big twist on werewolves and vampires myth and ambitious world building, I am pretty sure The Others series has the most original concept in genre right now. There is nothing like it out there and it's the idea Bishop is pitching successfully to readers third year in a row.:)<br/>**************************<br/><br/>With second book we finally took a step out of Courtyard to see a bigger picture of Namid's world. That added new layers to story since we became aware that there are m</span>
  <span id="freeText14304273570674307329" style="display:none">3,5 stars<br /><br /> With unlike heroine, big twist on werewolves and vampires myth and ambitious world building, I am pretty sure The Others series has the most original concept in genre right now. There is nothing like it out there and it's the idea Bishop is pitching successfully to readers third year in a row.:)<br />**************************<br /><br />With second book we finally took a step out of Courtyard to see a bigger picture of Namid's world. That added new layers to story since we became aware that there are more parties inhabiting these territories (Intuitus) and that arrangement between Others and humans is not really working. It's a ticking bomb waiting to blow up, as we saw it happened in Thasia, in Jerzy area.<br />This book deals with effects of Meg's staying in Courtyard and her influence on Others and how it changed the dynamics between humans and terra indigene in times when tensions and incidents all around the world are becoming more frequent and more violent. <br />As we know, Meg gained trust and protection of Others by preventing several bad incidents with her premonitions. She became a pack and their friend. She opened Simon Wolfguard's eyes to the fact that not all humans are thinking bad and only worth to be considered food, which resulted in cooperation with human police (Burke and Montgomery) and allowing other humans access to parts of Courtyard and parts of their lives that were strictly forbidden to them. <br />Events of MoC, when humans made their first serious move against terra indigene creating two powerful drugs, left Others wary and distrustful more than ever. And not just that- older, native terra indigene who live in wild lands are keeping close eye on humans after what they did, so Simon and rest of BA know that with new conflict HFL is gunning for, they can decide to erase humans completely from Thasia. There is also an issue of recovered cassandra sangue who are still vulnerable, so Meg is trying to come up with solution that will help them cope and come up with sensory overload and their addiction to cutting. <br /><br />Ok, Meg was never my favorite heroine, since she lacks moral complexity (any complexity, in fact) that would make her more unpredictable and able to surprise me, but I understand why author made her that way. Through her innocent, unbiased and inexperienced pov, we are able to get true, filterless picture of what's going on. Humans, the way Others know them, are either stupid and meat or cunning and manipulative, so they can only provoke one reactions with in them: distrust. But Meg, the way she is, makes a believable catalyst for change in their opinion that all humans are only meat. <br />There are some developments in Simon's character since he is trying to maintain this delicate balance and help humans who are considered friends. There is full on segregation going on because of HFL (Humans First and Last movement), so anyone who is working with Courtyard suffers the brunt of it. It struck me that, as much as he kept his inhuman and utterly wolfish nature throughout entire novel, he pulled some serious political moves and made progressive changes that are not typical for terra indigene. <br />Anyone who is looking forward to romance development, I have to disappoint you- nothing yet. In fact, it was less obvious than ever and, frankly, considering Meg's fragile mental state, her lack of experience and troubles they are dealing with, I am more comfortable this way.<br /><br />I chucked the star off because this reads like "build up" piece- Beside major moves, all characters are also performing these little,mundane, everyday tasks.It felt dragged out or, maybe, with third book, novelty of Meg's work in liaison office, pony's stumping, Skippy's antics, etc. is simply not as riveting for me as it was first time around. But, while reading all these scenes, I couldn't shake off the feeling there is something huge coming up. Like there is a lot of things going on but everything that's happening in this book is only teasing the real conflict in the future.<br />I hope in next book, we'll finally get to read about Cel-Romano, since it's a place controlled by humans- I am curious how's that working. I think terra indigene can expect upcoming attack from them since everything is pointing toward the fact they are gathering troupes. Drugs that affect Others, food supplies and humans always had numbers on their side- war is coming. :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14304273570674307329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1018025417" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1018025417" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408028716p2/17295220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1018025417?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101635117" href="/book/show/25083430-vision-in-silver">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17295220-alexa?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1018025417" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3982742343607265625"><b>I’m not sure why I gave this one the same rating as the last two.</b><br/><br/>It’s still good and I pretty much inhaled it the minute it was released, but it had several problems, the first being that things start getting repetitive, like these kinds of comments: <br/><blockquote><i>“cassandra sangue retained the sweetness of a child’s heart,”</i> or <br/><br/><i>“they were Namid’s creation, both wondrous and terrible,”</i></blockquote><br/>You told me already, let’s move on!<br/><br/>My other problem with the book is that it tries to fix a plot problem by reversing character</span>
  <span id="freeText3982742343607265625" style="display:none"><b>I’m not sure why I gave this one the same rating as the last two.</b><br /><br />It’s still good and I pretty much inhaled it the minute it was released, but it had several problems, the first being that things start getting repetitive, like these kinds of comments: <br /><blockquote><i>“cassandra sangue retained the sweetness of a child’s heart,”</i> or <br /><br /><i>“they were Namid’s creation, both wondrous and terrible,”</i></blockquote><br />You told me already, let’s move on!<br /><br />My other problem with the book is that it tries to fix a plot problem by reversing character development. Meg has been a strong character in her own way so far; she escaped the compound, found the others, got a job, learned to cook, drive, make friends, etc. <br /><br />Now suddenly OUT OF NOWHERE, she’s having meltdowns every few chapters because “she can’t cope with change.” Are you fucking kidding me? -.-<br /><br />The real reason she’s having meltdowns is because the other Cassandra Sangue that were released in the last book are having meltdowns and they need Meg to have some too, so she can explain how to deal with them. It just didn’t make sense for the progression of the character and annoyed me SO MUCH.<br /><br />Also, there’s still no romance. Which wouldn’t usually be a problem for me but the author keeps hinting at it and it is starting to grate on my nerves.<br /><br />The plot follows the ideas planted by the past two books about the conflict between the Terra Indigene and the Humans First and Last movement. So far our new villain, Nicholas Scratch, seems to be just as distant and non-involved as the controller and while I enjoy the book, I miss having a villain that I can hate. I’m also still curious to see if future books will show us a bit of the conflict that’s happening in the Cel Romano Alliance of Nations. (Pretty please?)<br /><br />I was really interested in the new Cassandra Sangue girl they added and hopefully we’ll be seeing more of her.<br /><br />PS. I don't like this cover. Meg looks weird. Also, her hair should be short!<br /><br /><i>Re-read in Feb 2016 for the release of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22062202.Marked_in_Flesh__The_Others___4_" title="Marked in Flesh (The Others, #4) by Anne Bishop" rel="nofollow noopener">Marked in Flesh</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3982742343607265625" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KNhsCJvrOozz+qVWng11MURtxg5/jEg94GLtsIE7j+bckZ4tQllz5xCQ2q2tFGvPsiNZEzHFa69mxUTXAoPLiQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TMbhf5VgPT0ynmZo8jp9cMqOYHOEkdbAtKv7P5Jhzfm4jxNaTNJ0VtH0GZPBI2OOPMD/bsrY9VIyDFJYEdmJlg==')})
  }
